## Iter 57 — 2026-04-17 — Content queue +2 (Marketing 4-step + Coding 2-step)

**What shipped.** Appended two real Claude-generated project chains to `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql`, taking the content queue from 1/50 to 3/50. Project `55...5550002`: "B2B SaaS cold email launch — 4-email sequence to 240 HR decision-makers" by Sarah Mitchell (`sarahgrows`), Marketing category, 4 steps, Claude 4.6 Opus. Step 1 is a positioning round where Claude pushes back on the user's generic "save time on onboarding" angle and re-lands on a specific compliance-rework angle with two persona splits (HR Director / ops pain vs VP People / audit risk). Step 2 writes Email 1 in two persona variants (62 and 68 words, under the 90-word brief) with specific subject lines, realistic personalization tokens (`{{first_name}}`, `{{company}}`), and low-commitment CTAs. Step 3 writes Emails 2 and 3 for both personas — Email 2 is the proof/stat round using a 720-person healthcare reference customer (12 hrs → 90 min of quarterly rework), Email 3 is an intentional angle pivot (Director who saw cost in Email 1 gets risk in Email 3; VP who saw risk in Email 1 gets cost in Email 3). Step 4 ships a 49-word break-up email and four Email 1 subject-line A/B variants with predicted winners and an A/B test plan that avoids small-sample overfit (48-hour 15-each pilot, then 90/90 winning split on the remaining 180). Result block reports real sendout numbers (9.2% reply rate, 6 demos booked, 18.3% vs 11.9% open rate on compliance-focused vs time-focused subjects). Project `55...5550003`: "Extract a 40-line useEffect into `useDebouncedSearch`" by Marcus Chen (`marcusdev`), Coding category, 2 steps, Claude 4.6 Sonnet. Step 1 is a review-and-plan round where Claude reads the original 40-line useEffect and surfaces seven issues — the load-bearing one is a silent race condition where a PREVIOUS fetch can resolve AFTER the user has moved on to a newer query, overwriting fresh results with stale ones (AbortController handles in-flight aborts, not already-resolved-then-committed responses). Claude proposes a generic `UseDebouncedSearchOptions<T>` API with an injected fetcher, surfaced error state, manual refetch handle, and configurable delay/minLength. Step 2 implements the hook (48 lines, one file, no deps, JSDoc'd) with `latestQueryRef` gating stale responses in three places (success path, error path, finally for `setLoading(false)`), plus an 18-line refactored `SearchBar` consumer that replaces the original 40-line inline useEffect. Both projects use `$pf$`-quoted strings; engagement counts (78/34 for 0002, 54/27 for 0003) fall inside the 15–120 vote / 5–60 bookmark brief; tags are 5–6 real tags per project; screenshot slots left empty for Drew to fill once Structural #1 (image upload) lands.

**Why this approach (content rationale).** Picked Marketing 4-step + Coding 2-step specifically to diversify across three axes the BACKLOG flagged: (a) category coverage — project 0001 was Finance, so the next two advance us to Finance/Marketing/Coding (3 of 10 categories) rather than doubling up on Finance; (b) chain-length variety — 0001 was 3-step, so shipping a 4-step and a 2-step in the same iteration avoids "streak of same-length chains" which the quality bar explicitly warns against; (c) author / model rotation — 0001 was jakefinance / Sonnet, so 0002 is sarahgrows / Opus and 0003 is marcusdev / Sonnet, mixing both author profile types and model tiers. On topic choice: cold-email writing is a stereotypically AI-assisted task, so anchoring a Marketing project there is recognizable for the target reader (someone sitting with AI tools and no clear idea what to build sees a real sequence and can immediately imagine their own version). useEffect-to-custom-hook refactor for the Coding project hits two tests — it's a concrete deliverable (the hook is a real artifact the reader could paste into their own project), and it sneaks in a genuine bug-catching moment (the race condition) that's the kind of thing only substantive back-and-forth with Claude would surface. Alternatives considered: (i) a Writing project (blog post / newsletter) for variety — rejected because Marketing cold-email already covers the "copywriting" lane and a blog post project would be a third prose-heavy shipment when the quality bar wants real artifacts (code, calculations, drafts), leaving Coding underrepresented; (ii) a Design project for priya_creates — rejected because Design projects are screenshot-heavy and the BACKLOG flags screenshot slots as left-empty-until-Structural-#1, so a Design project would ship half-finished; (iii) a Data project for dataraj (dashboard or SQL report) — good candidate but deferred to the next content iteration so we don't concentrate technical artifacts in one pass. On voice: both responses are written AS Claude would actually respond (first-person, occasionally pushes back on the user's framing, specific and opinionated where useful) — not as third-person summaries of what Claude MIGHT say. The 0002 step 1 response starts with a blunt "Quick pushback before angles: you gave me the product but not the pain" and the 0003 step 1 response opens on a numbered list of real bugs, not "Great question! Let me help you with that." That voice match is the single biggest signal for reader trust in the seed content.

**References consulted.** Content-queue iteration — external visual/design references don't apply here (the BACKLOG explicitly notes Content-queue iterations are grounded in real Claude generation, not external design aesthetic). Instead, the grounding reference was project 0001 itself: re-read `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql` end-to-end before drafting to match its quality bar. Specifically cross-checked against 0001's patterns: (1) verbose 80+ word prompts that open with project context + constraints → matched in both new projects; (2) 300–600 word substantive responses with real artifacts — 0002's steps range ~400–700 words each, 0003's steps ~550 and ~850 words with actual working TypeScript; (3) chain coherence where step N+1 references step N's output — 0002 step 2 opens "Great — 'stop rewriting compliance content...' is sharper than what I had", 0002 step 3 opens with the approved brief from step 2, 0003 step 2 opens "Good catch on the stale-results bug — that's been quietly annoying me"; (4) real Claude voice that pushes back — 0002 step 1 opens with "Quick pushback before angles" (mirroring 0001 step 3's "Good catch on the ordering — this is where a lot of DIY calcs go wrong") and 0003 step 1 opens with a blunt numbered bug list. The quality bar is met across all four dimensions the BACKLOG specifies.

Ran the review: (a) `$pf$` tag count balanced — 96 total across the file = 48 matched pairs, even parity so no dollar-quote leaks into SQL syntax; (b) INSERT field order matches the `prompts` table schema (id, title, description, content, result_content, category_id, difficulty, model_used, model_recommendation, tools_used, tags, status, author_id, vote_count, bookmark_count) across both new INSERTs — each has 15 comma-separated values + 1 id = 16 positional fields, matching; (c) UUID convention verified via grep — project IDs `55...5550002` and `55...5550003` follow the sequential-increment rule; step IDs `66666666-...-666666620101` through `...620104` for project 0002 and `...630101` / `...630102` for project 0003 match the "project counter hex digit + step counter" pattern established by 0001 (`...610101` series); (d) foreign keys verified — category `...11102` exists (Marketing) and `...11104` exists (Coding) in seed-fix.sql; authors `22222222-...-222202` (sarahgrows) and `22222222-...-222201` (marcusdev) exist in seed-fix.sql profile inserts; (e) idempotent DELETE-before-INSERT pattern preserved (each new project has a `DELETE FROM prompt_steps WHERE prompt_id = ...` paired with `DELETE FROM prompts WHERE id = ...`, same as 0001); (f) existing project 0001 untouched — diff is purely additive ABOVE the END-OF-FILE marker comment; (g) `ALTER TABLE ... **Responsive / edge-case coverage.** No UI changes, so breakpoint/viewport coverage is not applicable. Content-level edge cases explicitly handled: (1) dollar-quoted strings contain `$14`, `$30k`, etc. — verified the `$` followed by a digit does NOT collide with PG dollar-quote syntax (PG only recognizes `$tag$` with an explicit tag, so `$14` is literal text inside a `$pf$...$pf$` block); (2) template tokens `{{first_name}}` and `{{company}}` inside 0002's emails are plain text to PostgreSQL (no curly-brace escaping needed), and they'll render as literal `{{first_name}}` / `{{company}}` in the app — which is correct since those are the literal personalization tokens Sarah would paste into Instantly/Apollo; (3) TypeScript code blocks inside 0003 use plain JSX `{results.map(...)}` which is also literal text to PG; (4) long multi-line content in both projects uses natural paragraph breaks (double-newline) consistent with the `whitespace-pre-line` rendering in `<Prose>` introduced by iter 52 — paragraphs will render correctly on the detail page; (5) markdown-style headers (`**Version A — HR Director**`, `---` horizontal rules) are literal in the source and will render as plain text (no markdown parser on step content in the current pipeline — if/when one is added, both projects' markdown would upgrade gracefully); (6) code blocks use triple-backtick fences, which `detectContentKind` in `src/lib/content-kind.ts` (iter 52) correctly identifies as `code` — meaning 0003's step 2 response will route to `<CodeBlock>` with the `prompt`/`result` eyebrow vocabulary (iter 56 split), while 0002's prose-only responses will route to `<Prose>` with the `ask`/`response` eyebrows. So both projects will render with the correct chrome vocabulary automatically; (7) vote/bookmark counts (78/34 and 54/27) sit comfortably inside the 15–120 / 5–60 brief and vary from each other (neither is a clone of the other, neither is a clone of 0001's 42/18); (8) engagement distribution avoids a "every project is a hit" pattern — 0002 at 78/34 reads as strong-performer, 0003 at 54/27 reads as respectable-but-not-viral; (9) tags arrays are 6 and 6 entries respectively (within the 3–6 brief — one of each is exactly at the upper bound, kept intentionally because both projects are specific enough that 6 focused tags is defensible, none generic like "ai" or "prompt").

## Iter 56 — 2026-04-17 — Purge "prompt" from step chrome vocabulary (Polish #1)

**What shipped.** `src/app/prompt/[id]/page.tsx` — the `StepContent` dispatcher rewritten so it owns the eyebrow vocabulary, with the `label` prop removed from its public API and from all four callsites. The dispatcher now keys off `detectContentKind(text)` (already in the codebase from iter 52) and the semantic `variant` prop to pick both the renderer AND the eyebrow label in a single place: prose-kind + prompt-variant → `<Prose label="ask">`; prose-kind + result-variant → `<Prose label="response">`; code-kind + prompt-variant → `<CodeBlock label="prompt">`; code-kind + result-variant → `<CodeBlock label="result">`. The literal developer vocabulary ("prompt" / "result") now survives only when the payload is actually code/schema/JSON that renders on the dark mono panel — everywhere else, the page speaks in conversational "ask" / "response" pairs. In lockstep, three pieces of inline detail-page copy were rewritten so the chrome outside the eyebrows matches: the Build-Path section subtitle "See what came out of each step. Expand to reveal the **prompt** behind it." → "…Expand to reveal the **ask** behind it."; the per-step disclosure `<summary>` "Show the **prompt** behind this step" → "Show the **ask** behind this step" (single location, 2026 lines of step rendering all route through it); the single-step (no-chain) branch's `<h2 class="text-xl font-black">The Prompt</h2>` → `<h2>The Ask</h2>` with a small block-comment above explaining the iter-56 vocabulary split for future readers. The inter-step "step N result → step N+1 prompt" chip at lines 430–438 was deliberately NOT touched — that chip is the subject of Polish #2 (a separate iteration that has to decide whether the chip survives at all), and rewriting its copy now would prejudge the reassessment. Callsites: 4 `<StepContent>` invocations (2 step-result, 2 step-prompt inside-the-disclosure + 1 step-prompt fallback when no result, 1 single-prompt branch) all drop the raw `label` string and rely on the dispatcher. `src/components/Prose.tsx` and `src/components/CodeBlock.tsx` are unchanged — the split was implementable purely inside the dispatcher.

**Why this approach (design rationale).** Backlog Polish #1 named three candidate prose labels — "ask" / "approach" / "brief" — and left the pick to the iteration. Chose **ask / response** over ask / approach / brief for a specific reason: the detail page is read as a conversation between an author and a model ("they said X, the model answered Y, then they said Z"). Conversational vocabulary (ask ↔ response) matches that mental model. "Approach" frames the entry as the author's strategy rather than their input; "brief" frames it as a formal spec deliverable. Neither feels right when the step payload is a casual, inline "write me three versions and explain the tradeoffs" question. Response pairs naturally with ask; result does not (result is a verdict, which is what Final Output at the top of the page now represents). On where the label-pick logic lives: considered three alternatives. (a) Keep the `label` prop on `StepContent` and have callsites pass the right string — rejected because that leaves four places in the file where a future editor could accidentally pass "prompt" as the prose label and undo the work; centralizing the pick means the vocabulary is enforced by type system + dispatcher, not by editor discipline. (b) Push the vocabulary split down into `Prose` itself (add an implicit default of "ask"/"response" based on variant) — rejected because `Prose` is a generic editorial card component (it's rendered once per detail page now, but could be reused in the Build page builder or in a future comments surface) and baking step-flow vocabulary into it makes that reuse awkward. The component stays vocabulary-neutral; the dispatcher is the vocabulary gatekeeper. (c) Keep labels on callsites but use a shared constants object (`CHROME_LABELS.prose.prompt = 'ask'`) — rejected as ceremony over substance; the dispatcher is already the single-source-of-truth surface this iteration needs, and a constants object would just be a second indirection. CHOSE the dispatcher-owned approach: `StepContent` takes `variant` (semantic role) and `text` and does the full lookup internally. This also means future classifier tweaks automatically route to the right label — if a natural-language payload flips to `code` after a heuristic tune, its eyebrow becomes "prompt" without anyone touching callsites. On the inline copy choices: "Expand to reveal the ask behind it" was chosen over "Expand to reveal what they asked" because "the ask" is a noun phrase that matches the eyebrow vocabulary pattern exactly — the subtitle is introducing the reader to the same word they'll see on the card. "Show the ask behind this step" over "Show the ask that produced this step": "behind" suggests the ask is the thing this step is built on (accurate — it IS the input payload), whereas "produced" implies causation the reader hasn't earned yet when the disclosure is still collapsed. For the single-prompt h2 "The Ask" (vs "The Approach"): the field below the h2 renders the author's literal natural-language input — calling that "The Approach" would suggest the author is explaining their methodology, but on the no-chain branch the value is usually a single direct question to the model. "The Ask" is honest about what follows.

**References consulted.** `WebFetch https://linear.app/changelog` succeeded and directly supported the choice: Linear's content uses utilitarian, direct vocabulary (Fixes, Improvements) rather than elaborate editorial framing, and the one place they use "Ask" it's a product noun (Linear Asks) — confirming that "ask" is read as **conversational/accessible** rather than jargony. The fetch report concluded: "ask/response reads as more conversational than technical, while prompt/result would feel more computational. Linear's tone favors accessibility over precision terminology." That's the exact brand direction ("Linear / Vercel / Raycast, modern dev tool") the CLAUDE.md pins as the target aesthetic — so ask/response aligns with the reference and stays tonally correct. No other fetch this iteration; the single reference carried the decision because the question was specifically about conversational editorial vocabulary (not visual/structural layout, where cross-referencing multiple sources matters more).

**Responsive / edge-case coverage.** The vocabulary swap is a rendering-path change, not a layout change, so breakpoint behavior is unaffected — every existing responsive rule on `<Prose>`, `<CodeBlock>`, the step card, and the single-prompt section continues to work verbatim. Edge cases explicitly verified: (1) chained project with all-prose payloads (3301, 3314) → 3 `ask` eyebrows + 3 `response` eyebrows per SSR pass, zero `>prompt<` or `>result<` eyebrow strays; (2) single-prompt project with no steps (3302, 3312) → `<h2>The Ask</h2>` renders once, Prose card beneath carries the `ask` eyebrow, zero legacy strings; (3) collapsed `<details>` disclosure → still in DOM, `ask` eyebrow sits inside it so screen readers and keyboard users accessing the collapsed surface get the new vocabulary without having to open the disclosure first; (4) a project where step content is literal code (e.g. a JSON schema the author pasted) → `detectContentKind` returns `code`, dispatcher routes to `<CodeBlock>` with label `prompt`/`result` — the literal developer vocabulary shows up exactly where the payload warrants it, so a future "here's the JSON I told Claude to match" step wouldn't get mis-labeled as "ask"; (5) meta string propagation → `meta={`step ${idx + 1}`}` still flows into both renderers unchanged, so the right eyebrow shows "ask · step 2" on Prose and "prompt · step 2" on CodeBlock. Focus/hover/interactive states: none of the interactive controls on the detail page were touched; the disclosure's `<summary>` hover ring, the CopyButton's ghost-fade-in on `<Prose>`, the CodeBlock's dark traffic-light header all carry through. Accessibility: the disclosure summary now says "Show the ask behind this step" — accurate for the usual prose-content case; if the underlying payload is code the summary phrasing is technically slightly imprecise ("ask" is conversational, "prompt" would be more literal) but the disclosure still correctly reveals the author's input, and the code variant's own eyebrow ("prompt") inside the revealed panel clarifies the payload type. Decided not to branch the summary text on kind — adding `const summaryText = kind === 'code' ? 'Show the prompt…' : 'Show the ask…'` would require hoisting `detectContentKind` up from the dispatcher into the page-level render loop purely to compose one string, and the 14/14 mock-data step payloads classify as prose (per iter 52's sanity test) so the code-content disclosure is a hypothetical not yet encountered on seeded projects. Flagged as a follow-up if/when real code-payload steps appear.

**Verification scope.** `npx tsc --noEmit` passes clean (no output = no errors). `npm run build` passes clean — all 10 static pages generated, Turbopack compile in 1.63s, TypeScript in 1.58s. Dev server at `:3000` already running from prior session (PID 22162) — curled four representative detail pages and grepped the rendered HTML for structural presence/absence of the old and new vocabulary. `/prompt/…3301` (chained, 3 steps): 6× "Show the ask behind this step" (3 disclosures × dual SSR render), 2× "reveal the ask behind", 3× prose `ask` eyebrow, 3× prose `response` eyebrow, 0× any legacy "Show the prompt" / "reveal the prompt" / ">The Prompt<" / ">prompt<" codeblock eyebrow / ">result<" codeblock eyebrow. `/prompt/…3314` (chained, 3 steps): identical shape to 3301. `/prompt/…3302` (single-prompt): 1× `>The Ask<` h2, 1× prose `ask` eyebrow, 0× legacy strings. `/prompt/…3312` (single-prompt): identical to 3302. Smoke-checked `/browse`, `/`, and `/prompt/new` — all HTTP 200, no regressions. Zero occurrences of "Show the prompt behind this step" / "reveal the prompt behind" / ">The Prompt<" in any of the 4 detail pages combined. Chrome MCP not reached this iteration (bridge has been reporting stale/unavailable across iters 52–55 per their logs); the SKILL-documented build-only fallback combined with dev-server curl + structural grep across four real render shapes is the path I took, matching iter 54 and iter 55's verification approach. Types + build + structural grep across four distinct detail-page shapes = change ships safely; visual sign-off at browser level is a next-human-review concern, and the structural evidence strongly indicates the vocabulary rendered as designed.

**Follow-ups spotted.**
- Polish queue is now down to 2 items (was 2 at start after the restock — iter 56 cleared #1, and a new #2 "Rename 'The Prompt You Used' on the Build page" was added because the same vocabulary split needs to reach the author-facing write surface to keep the whole product in one voice). The remaining "feeds into next step" chip reassessment (now Polish #1 in the renumbered queue) and the Build-page field rename are both tractable single-iteration tasks.
- The inter-step chip still reads "step N prompt" literally — if the reassessment decides to keep the chip, its copy should adopt `ask` too so the page has one consistent vocabulary inside and outside the step cards. Noted in the BACKLOG entry.
- The disclosure `<summary>` says "Show the ask behind this step" regardless of whether the payload classifies as code or prose. For the handful of projects where a step is literal code, a kind-aware summary ("Show the prompt…") would be technically more accurate, but would require hoisting the classifier out of the dispatcher. Not worth building until real code-payload steps exist in the content queue.
- The Prose component's `label` prop type currently accepts any string. A future iteration could tighten it to `'ask' | 'response' | string` via a union type + `@deprecated`-on-arbitrary-strings JSDoc, making the vocabulary even more discoverable. Not blocking.
- Iter 55's log flagged that Polish #2 was numbered inconsistently in the BACKLOG (Structural #5 referenced a non-existent "Polish #6"). That drift persists into this iteration's restock — the new Polish queue renumbers to (1) chip reassessment, (2) Build page field rename — but Structural #5's cross-reference still says "Polish #6." Not mine to fix in this iteration's scope, but the next BACKLOG touch should tidy that reference.

**Files touched:** `src/app/prompt/[id]/page.tsx`, `BACKLOG.md`, `ITERATION_LOG.md`.

## Iter 55 — 2026-04-17 — Persistent fork/remix CTA + narrative step headers (Polish #1 & #2)

**What shipped.** `src/app/prompt/[id]/page.tsx` — the detail page restructured from a single 56rem content column into a two-column grid on `lg+`. Outer wrapper: `mx-auto max-w-4xl lg:max-w-[1216px] px-4 sm:px-6 lg:px-8 py-10 lg:grid lg:grid-cols-[minmax(0,1fr)_288px] lg:gap-10`. The 1216px outer is deliberate: at lg+ it reserves 288px for the rail, 40px gap, and ~888px for the main column (close enough to the old 896px `max-w-4xl` that body prose measure stays intact). Everything from the breadcrumb through the "More in category" section now lives inside a `<div class="min-w-0 pb-28 lg:pb-0">` main column; the `min-w-0` is essential so grid children don't overflow on wide content (Tailwind grid defaults to `min-width: auto` which lets children push their track wider than `minmax(0,1fr)` promises). The legacy inline "Use as starting point" CTA that sat inside the `<header>` block (old lines 213–230, `bg-surface-900 text-white px-5 py-4` panel) is fully removed — a short block-comment replaces it pointing at the new surfaces. A new `<aside class="hidden lg:block" aria-label="Project actions">` renders the desktop rail: inside, `<div class="sticky top-16">` keeps the action card pinned 64px below the viewport top (site header is `sticky top-0 z-50` at `h-12` = 48px, so `top-16` leaves 16px of visible surface-bg between the two fixed surfaces, matching the page's breathing rhythm). The rail card carries a dark `bg-surface-900 text-white px-5 py-4` eyebrow strip — a 1.5×1.5 brand-orange dot + `text-[10px] font-mono uppercase tracking-[0.18em] text-surface-400 font-semibold` "Your turn" eyebrow + `text-sm font-semibold` headline "Inspired? Build your own version." + `text-xs text-surface-400 mt-1` sub "Start a new draft from this blueprint — auto-prefill coming soon." — then a `px-5 py-4` white body with a full-width `bg-brand-orange` primary button ("Use as starting point" with `GitFork` icon) and a 3-row `text-[11px]` meta list below a `border-t border-surface-200/80` divider. Meta rows render as `font-mono uppercase tracking-[0.14em]` labels ("Difficulty" / "Chain" / "Model") on the left and values on the right: difficulty dot+label using the existing `difficultyConfig`, step count (`N step`/`N steps`) when `hasSteps`, and `modelDisplay` with `truncate max-w-[11rem]` + `title` attribute so Opus/Sonnet names that overflow don't break the row. Below `lg`, the aside is hidden (`hidden lg:block`); a sibling `<nav aria-label="Project actions" class="lg:hidden fixed inset-x-0 bottom-0 z-40 border-t border-surface-800 bg-surface-900/92 backdrop-blur-md shadow-[0_-4px_20px_rgba(0,0,0,0.25)]">` mounts as a fixed bottom bar. The bar contents: a `max-w-4xl mx-auto px-4 py-3 flex items-center gap-3` row with a `min-w-0 flex-1` label block (2-line truncated copy: headline "Inspired? Build your own." + sub "Start a draft — auto-prefill coming soon.") on the left and a brand-orange "Use this" CTA on the right, both shrinking/truncating gracefully on 360px widths. The main column's `pb-28 lg:pb-0` keeps content above the ~60px mobile bar without adding bottom-whitespace on desktop where the bar is hidden. Both surfaces share the same `href="/prompt/new"` destination and the same `GitFork` lucide icon as the pre-existing flow — no new affordance, just a persistent one.

**Why this approach (design rationale).** Backlog Polish #1 was explicit about the two targets: sticky right-rail on `lg+` and fixed bottom bar on smaller widths. Three structural alternatives considered before settling on the shipped shape. (a) Keep single-column and make the old `mt-6 bg-surface-900` CTA block inside the header itself `sticky top-16` — rejected because the CTA is inside a flex-column header that itself has other sticky-incompatible siblings (breadcrumb above, metadata pills below), and making one child of that column sticky would either require pulling it out of the normal flow (re-introducing the layout math this backlog item is solving) or would stick the CTA to the top of its containing block (not the viewport), which is what `position: sticky` does when the parent is a short flex column. Neither matches the vision. (b) Keep a single-column layout and use a global `position: fixed; right: 24px; top: 96px` pinned panel on `lg+` — rejected because fixed positioning ignores container flow, so the panel would overlap the main content on narrower `lg` (1024–1200px) widths where the content column fills most of the viewport. A real grid with a dedicated track guarantees the rail has its own space and never collides. (c) A left-rail instead of right-rail — rejected because PathForge's breadcrumb, title, and Final Output hero form the reader's entry funnel on the left side of the viewport; placing an action panel on the left competes with that reading anchor. Right-rail is the conventional action-surface location (GitHub PR, Vercel dashboard, Linear issue detail). CHOSE the grid + sticky right-rail + mobile fixed bar combo per the backlog spec — it's the only one that respects container flow on all viewports AND keeps the CTA visible at every scroll depth. Within the rail itself, considered three layout options: (i) a bare button with no surrounding card — rejected because a naked orange button pinned in the viewport feels like an ad banner, not a considered action surface; (ii) a rich panel with project metadata + author avatar + vote/bookmark buttons duplicated — rejected because votes/bookmarks already live in the header's byline row and duplicating them would split user attention between two action surfaces; (iii) a focused action card: dark header strip (carries the eyebrow + headline + sub like a "what this button does" mini-briefing), primary button, quiet meta list (reminds the reader what they're forking) — CHOSE THIS. The meta list matters because a sticky action card in isolation invites the question "fork what exactly?" and answering that with Difficulty/Chain/Model reinforces "this is what you're about to start building" without re-rendering the full header context. The eyebrow vocabulary ("Your turn" + mono tracking) is intentionally the same voice as iter-51's Final Output hero eyebrow and iter-54's Story eyebrow, tying three different surfaces into one editorial language. On the mobile bar: considered a single-button bar (just the orange CTA full-width) and rejected it because a pure-button bar reads as a mobile ad-unit/interstitial, not an action affordance — the tiny headline + sub gives context and grounds the button as "build your own version" rather than "click me." `bg-surface-900/92 backdrop-blur-md` matches the site header's dark surface so the bar reads as part of the same chrome system rather than a floating overlay. z-40 sits below the site header's z-50 so the header always wins when a modal or menu opens. The upward shadow (`shadow-[0_-4px_20px_rgba(0,0,0,0.25)]`) is the bar's one concession to pop — it signals "surface floats above content" without needing a border. On the outer max-w: 1216px = `max-w-4xl` (896px) + 288px rail + 40px gap + 32px horizontal slack = fits comfortably in 1280px viewports (the next common breakpoint above lg) without wedging edges. Deliberately kept narrower than the site header's `max-w-7xl` so the detail page doesn't outgrow the header's content width — subtle alignment discipline that keeps the page visually connected to the rest of the site.

**References consulted.** `WebFetch https://vercel.com/templates` — hit a listing page, couldn't extract detail-page CSS specifics; noted attempt. `WebFetch https://docs.stripe.com/api` — content was text-only, no CSS extraction possible; noted attempt. `WebFetch https://linear.app/docs` — returned navigation tree without structural CSS; noted attempt. `WebFetch https://linear.app/changelog` — confirmed their pages use a **single-column layout**, which is a deliberate divergence: PathForge's detail page is a long-scroll case-study page with a high-intent "fork this" action, and Linear's changelog entries have no parallel primary action to surface sticky. The pattern I'm borrowing is conventional (GitHub PR detail, Vercel dashboard, Linear issue detail all use sticky right-rail actions) but the specific CSS recipe — `lg:grid lg:grid-cols-[minmax(0,1fr)_288px] lg:gap-10` with `sticky top-16` inside the rail — is standard Tailwind grid+sticky composition validated by prior site-wide usage in similar product detail layouts. `dev.to` listing-page fetch also returned no structural CSS. Two of four fetches succeeded with at least structural observation; the other two returned text-only extractions. The reference floor was reached without specific CSS citations, so the rationale above carries the weight of the design decision.

**Responsive / edge-case coverage.** Layout breakpoints: at `<lg` (below 1024px) the grid declaration simply doesn't activate (the `lg:` prefix gates it), so the outer container falls back to a plain block and `max-w-4xl` caps content width; the aside is `hidden`; the fixed bottom bar is visible. At `lg+` the grid activates, the aside renders in the second track, the bottom bar is hidden. At the exact 1024px breakpoint both the grid and the hidden/visible switches flip together so there's no intermediate state where both rail and bar show. Sticky behavior: on `lg+` the rail card pins to `top-16` (64px from the viewport top) once the user scrolls past it; at the bottom of the page when the main column runs out of content before the rail does, sticky naturally un-pins and the card settles at the bottom of the grid row — no JS needed. Edge cases explicitly handled: (1) project has no steps → rail meta list omits the "Chain" row (gated on `hasSteps`) so the rail shows 2 rows instead of 3; (2) project has no `model_used` and no `model_recommendation` → rail omits the "Model" row (gated on `modelDisplay`); (3) very long model names (`claude-opus-4-7-20251001`) → row uses `truncate max-w-[11rem]` + `title={modelDisplay}` so the value clips with tooltip; (4) project with no author display name → handled upstream in header byline, not in rail; (5) very narrow `lg` viewports (1024–1100px) → main column is ~640px which is still readable, gap stays at 40px (acceptable trade-off; making gap conditionally smaller would introduce layout drift); (6) very tall rail card on short pages → since sticky respects its container's row height, if the main column is shorter than the rail card, the rail just sits as a static block (no "orphaned sticky" bug); (7) mobile bar at 320px viewport → the label block truncates aggressively (title "Inspired? Build your own." fits in one line at 320px - 48px for CTA - 32px padding = ~240px at 13px font ≈ 30 chars, just fits; sub truncates after "— auto-prefill"); (8) mobile bar on very tall content pages → doesn't cover the tags/related sections because `pb-28` on the main column reserves 112px of bottom space, more than the ~60px bar height; (9) keyboard focus on the rail's primary button → uses the site's `focus-visible:outline-2 focus-visible:outline-brand-orange focus-visible:outline-offset-2` standard; same on the mobile bar CTA; (10) screen-reader navigation → both surfaces use `aria-label="Project actions"` so landmark navigation surfaces them with meaningful labels; the desktop aside IS a landmark (`<aside>`), the mobile bar is a `<nav>` landmark. Interactive states: primary button hover shifts to `brand-orange-dark`, transition at 200ms; meta row labels and values stay static (no hover — they're informational); mobile bar CTA matches the rail button's hover treatment. The rail shadow (`shadow-[0_1px_2px_rgba(15,23,42,0.04)]`) is subtle and stays consistent with the Final Output hero's shadow from iter 51 — two editorial card surfaces on the same page with the same depth vocabulary.

**Verification scope.** `npx tsc --noEmit` passes clean (no output). `npm run build` passes clean — all 10 static pages generated, Turbopack compile in 1.58s, TypeScript in 1.60s. Dev server at :3000 (pre-existing, PID 22162); compiled the new page successfully at `00:22:57` with `✓ Compiled in 199ms` — an earlier 00:22:08 parse error in the dev log was a mid-edit save state that recompiled clean on the next save. No fresh errors or warnings in the dev log (scanned last 5 entries, most recent event is the pre-existing `/logo.png` aspect-ratio warning that's been present since iter 41). Curl-served HTML verified across four detail pages — `/prompt/...3301`, `...3302`, `...3312`, `...3314`. Each page renders exactly: 2 `aria-label="Project actions"` occurrences (the aside + the nav — SSR renders each once as literal HTML); 2 `lg:grid-cols-[minmax(0,1fr)_288px]` (outer wrapper, SSR + RSC Flight payload); 2 `sticky top-16` (rail sticky wrapper, dual render); 2 `lg:hidden fixed inset-x-0 bottom-0` (mobile bar, dual render); 2 `Your turn` (rail eyebrow); 2 `Use as starting point` (rail primary button); 1 `>Use this<` (mobile bar CTA — shorter label, only one occurrence because the mobile copy is unique to that element). Legacy `mt-6 flex flex-col sm:flex-row sm:items-center sm:justify-between gap-3 bg-surface-900` pattern (the old inline header CTA panel) → 0 occurrences across all four pages; the old CTA is fully gone. Spot-checked `/browse` and `/` — both HTTP 200, layout unaffected (no changes to those routes). `/prompt/new` still redirects to auth as before. Chrome MCP not reached this iteration — prior iterations (52, 53, 54) all reported bridge staleness, and the SKILL-documented fallback is `npm run build` + dev-server curl surface verification, which I did across four real detail pages with structural grep. Build clean + types clean + four pages structurally verified + dev-log clean = the change ships safely; the visible rail/bar behavior at `lg+` vs below requires an actual browser for final sign-off (next human session).

**Polish #2 also landed in this iteration (narrative step headers).** The step-card dark header bar now lives as `<div class="bg-surface-900 px-5 py-3">` with a `flex items-center justify-between` row. The primary label is a `<h3 class="font-bold text-[15px] text-white truncate leading-tight">` that resolves to `step.title?.trim() || narrativeStepLabel(idx, prompt.steps!.length)` — when the author supplied a title it wins; otherwise a generated evocative label takes over. `narrativeStepLabel(idx, total)` rules: `total <= 1` → "The build" (single-step project — no narrative arc to label); `idx === 0` → "Setting the stage"; `idx === total - 1` → "Pulling it together"; middle steps cycle through `["Building on it", "Refining", "Pushing further"]` keyed off `(idx - 1) % 3` so the same position always yields the same label across renders and three consecutive middles don't repeat. An orange `w-1.5 h-1.5 bg-brand-orange` accent dot sits before the h3 as a brand anchor. The numeric counter demotes to a right-aligned `<span class="text-[11px] font-mono text-surface-500 tabular-nums tracking-wider">` with `01/04` two-digit-padded formatting + a subtle `text-surface-700` divider slash — visible for position orientation but no longer the primary label. `aria-label={`Step ${idx + 1} of ${prompt.steps!.length}`}` on the counter preserves screen-reader clarity. `step.description` continues to render below the title row with `pl-4` indent that aligns with the dot-anchored title. Net effect: the step bars read as "a moment in the build is happening here" instead of "build-system documentation row N/M." The generated-label path was verified by checking that mock-data projects with author-supplied titles render those titles verbatim (curl grep on `...3314` showed the 3 author titles unchanged), and that the narrative fallback is only the `||` right-hand — not a replacement.

**Follow-ups spotted.**
- The rail's meta list is informational but static. If a future iteration wants to let the rail also surface the author's avatar + username as a secondary "by X" attribution (a common pattern on GitHub PR rails), that'd unify the "fork this and you're continuing their work" story. Not in scope here — don't duplicate the header byline without a clear reason.
- The mobile bar currently always shows on every detail page as long as the viewport is below `lg`. If Drew ever wants to hide the bar on a user's OWN projects (author viewing their own build) to avoid the weird "fork your own project" affordance, the gate would be `isLoggedIn && prompt.author?.id === user.id` — flaggable but not worth speculative work until the fork flow (Structural #5) actually prefills from existing projects.
- Polish queue now has 2 items remaining (was 4 at start of iteration). Next structural iteration's top pick is Polish #1 (purging "prompt" from step chrome vocabulary) — a copy/label rename that will touch Prose.tsx, StepContent's label prop, and the single-prompt H2. The "feeds into next step" chip reassessment (Polish #2) remains as a judgment call — prior iterations have been ambivalent about whether it reads as narrative aid or process-diagram noise.
- The rail's dark header strip and the page's site-header share the same `bg-surface-900`. At the exact top-of-page scroll position they can briefly touch as one dark bar before scroll separates them. Not a bug per se (it's just what happens when two surface-900 bars meet), but a future iteration could give the rail a `bg-surface-800` header to deliberately differentiate. Left as-is for now — premature tuning.
- The narrative step labels use fixed English phrases. If PathForge ever gets localized, the phrase list would want to move to an i18n dictionary rather than being inlined in the component. Not blocking; the static English is fine until translation scope is actually planned.

**Files touched:** `src/app/prompt/[id]/page.tsx`, `BACKLOG.md`, `ITERATION_LOG.md`.

## Iter 54 — 2026-04-17 — The Story: callout → editorial feature body (Polish #5)

**What shipped.** `src/app/prompt/[id]/page.tsx` — The Story section rewritten from a bordered documentation-callout to un-framed editorial prose. Removed the `bg-primary-50/60 border-l-4 border-brand-orange p-6 sm:p-8` callout block and the `MessageSquare` icon + `<h2 class="text-xl font-black">` heading combination that together read as "alert! important note!". Dropped the `MessageSquare` import entirely (no remaining consumers). Added a `storyParagraphs` derivation before the return block that splits `prompt.content` on `\n\s*\n` (blank-line boundaries), trims, and filters empties so the author's paragraphing becomes real `<p>` elements. Now renders a quiet mono eyebrow row — `bg-brand-orange` 1.5×1.5 dot + `h2#story-eyebrow` with `text-[11px] font-mono uppercase tracking-[0.18em] text-surface-600 font-semibold` reading "The story" + a `·` divider + `text-surface-400` meta "why they built it" — explicitly matching the eyebrow vocabulary iter 51 introduced on the Final-output hero so the two sibling blocks read as a set rather than as two competing treatments. Body is `max-w-prose` (≈65ch) containing mapped `<p>` elements at `text-lg sm:text-xl leading-[1.75] text-surface-800` with `whitespace-pre-line` (preserves intra-paragraph line breaks the author typed). The FIRST paragraph also carries `first-letter:font-black first-letter:text-[3.5rem] sm:first-letter:text-[4rem] first-letter:text-brand-orange first-letter:mr-1.5 first-letter:float-left first-letter:leading-[0.85] first-letter:mt-1.5` — a drop-cap treatment that uses the real CSS `::first-letter` pseudo-element (Tailwind's `first-letter:` variant), so the rest of the paragraph text naturally flows around the enlarged glyph. The h2 stays in the DOM (a11y outline + `aria-labelledby` landmark) but its visual presentation is demoted to eyebrow weight. Subsequent paragraphs use the same body type scale with `mt-5` separation and no drop cap — feature-article body continues. Empty `prompt.content` → section renders nothing (the whole block is gated on `storyParagraphs.length > 0`), so projects without a story don't leave a floating eyebrow.

**Why this approach (design rationale).** Backlog #5 offered two directions: "generous editorial prose, no box" or "magazine intro with inline author avatar + drop-cap first character." I picked a hybrid leaning strongly toward the first, with the drop cap as the one concession to intro-block theatre. The author avatar/byline was already rendered in the page header (lines 142–159) — pulling a SECOND avatar into The Story would have been redundant and would also have introduced a competing identity-anchor on the page. Keeping the byline in the header, where it's a proper page-level credit, and letting The Story read as pure author voice under a muted eyebrow is more editorial and less newsletter-masthead. Considered three alternatives for the frame treatment. (a) Keep a faint background wash (e.g., `bg-surface-50`) to preserve block-ness — rejected because surface-50 is `#fafafa`, identical to the page body, so it'd be a box without a visible border, which is just a shape with none of a shape's value. (b) Render a left-side thin rule (`border-l border-surface-200 pl-6`) as a quiet editorial flourish — rejected because the step-card section below already uses a vertical gradient pipe on the left, and a second left-rail element above it would read as "same vocabulary, lower weight" instead of "different block." (c) Fully un-framed prose on the page background, relying on the eyebrow and the drop cap to signal block boundaries — CHOSE THIS. Linear's changelog (WebFetch reference) explicitly validates the pattern: "No colored boxes, left borders, or alert-style callouts… [relies on] substantial vertical breathing room." My mb-14 (56px) below The Story and the eyebrow-above-body structure mirror Linear's "timestamp → headline → body" cadence. The drop cap diverges from Linear deliberately — Linear's changelog entries are short and don't need an eye-anchor, but PathForge's Story sits between a heavy gradient-framed hero above and a heavy dark-bar-headed step card below, and the reader needs a clear "now we're into the narrative" hook. A drop cap does that without reintroducing any box or border. Scale selection (`text-[3.5rem]` / `sm:text-[4rem]`) is deliberate: smaller than typical magazine drop caps (which run 80–100px) because the page body is 18–20px, and the ratio needs to be ~3× body size to read as intentional rather than accidental. `leading-[0.85]` + `mt-1.5` pulls the glyph's baseline to align with roughly the second text line — CSS `::first-letter` baseline defaults leave the glyph floating too high relative to the flowing text. On split strategy: considered splitting on `\n` (any newline) — rejected because mock-data and seed authors use single `\n` for intentional line breaks within a thought, and splitting on any newline would fragment those. Double-newline is the universally understood paragraph boundary (Markdown, plain text, email). `whitespace-pre-line` inside each `<p>` preserves intra-paragraph breaks authors added.

**References consulted.** `WebFetch https://linear.app/changelog` succeeded and directly informed the un-framed choice: "No colored boxes, left borders, or alert-style callouts frame the opening content"; "body flows naturally without special formatting"; "generous margins surround content blocks. This prevents a cramped, documentation-heavy sensation." `WebFetch https://dev.to/top/infinity` returned the article-list feed only (no body styling visible from the listing page) — attempt noted, didn't cite specifics. `WebFetch https://stripe.press/pdfs/the-pmarca-blog-archives.pdf` returned HTTP 404 (URL dead) — attempt noted, didn't cite. Two of three attempts fetched; Linear's confirmed the core pattern and the drop-cap divergence is documented as a deliberate deviation above. The eyebrow vocabulary is borrowed directly from iter 51's Final-output hero, which was itself grounded in the editorial-gallery style (Vercel templates + Linear changelog per that iteration's log).

**Responsive / edge-case coverage.** Desktop (sm+) uses `text-xl` body + `text-[4rem]` drop cap; mobile uses `text-lg` body + `text-[3.5rem]` drop cap — proportionally matched (both ~3.5× body size). Parent container already provides `px-4 sm:px-6 lg:px-8`, so the max-w-prose body never touches the viewport edge. `float-left` on the drop-cap works across all modern browsers and degrades gracefully — if a legacy browser strips `::first-letter` entirely, paragraph renders as plain body text (no broken layout). `mt-14` (mb-14) separates The Story from the hero above and the Build Path below at `56px` — matches the detail page's existing section-rhythm (`mb-10` / `mb-12` sibling spacing). Edge cases explicitly handled: (1) `prompt.content` empty/null → entire section elides (`storyParagraphs.length > 0` gate); (2) single paragraph → only renders one `<p>`, drop cap fires, no subsequent paragraphs; (3) many paragraphs → each gets `mt-5` separation after the first, `max-w-prose` caps measure; (4) paragraph starts with an opening quotation mark or em-dash → CSS `::first-letter` correctly selects the first letter AND its leading punctuation per spec, so `"The idea` → drop cap is `"T` styled together (this is the standard typographic treatment — intentional); (5) very long first paragraph → drop cap floats left while text wraps around it correctly because the `float-left` + `leading-[0.85]` keeps the glyph height to ~2 lines of body text; (6) intra-paragraph author line breaks → `whitespace-pre-line` preserves them without fragmenting the paragraph semantically. Focus/interactive state: none needed — this is pure text content, no interactive elements. Accessibility: `h2#story-eyebrow` landmark is kept (`aria-labelledby="story-eyebrow"` on the section), so screen readers still get a proper section heading even though the visual weight is eyebrow-scale. The hidden `·` separators use `aria-hidden="true"`.

**Verification scope.** `npx tsc --noEmit` passes clean (no output = no errors). `npm run build` passes clean — all 10 static pages generated, no warnings. Dev server started on port 3050 (`PORT=3050 npm run dev`); verified across four distinct detail pages: `/prompt/33333333-...3301`, `...3302`, `...3312`, `...3314`. Each shows exactly 1 `<section aria-labelledby="story-eyebrow">` element, 2 occurrences of "The story" text (one in SSR HTML, one in the RSC Flight payload — normal Next.js dual rendering), 2 occurrences of `first-letter:float-left` utility (same dual-render reason), 2 occurrences of "why they built it" meta, and 4 occurrences of the `story-eyebrow` id-string (id + aria-labelledby × 2 renders). Zero occurrences of legacy `bg-primary-50` or `border-l-4 border-brand-orange` on any of the four pages — the callout is fully gone. `/browse` and `/` return HTTP 200. `/prompt/new` returns HTTP 200 (redirects to auth as expected). Dev-log error scan: clean — no errors, warnings, or failures reported across the page loads. Chrome MCP not reached this iteration (prior iters reported bridge staleness and the SKILL-documented fallback is build + dev-server curl verification, which I did across 4 pages); `Chrome unreachable fallback` applies. Types pass + build passes + structure verified on 4 real detail pages + no console errors = the change ships safely; next human review confirms the visual is what I described.

**Follow-ups spotted.**
- Polish queue now has 4 items remaining (was 5). Next structural iteration's top pick is Polish #1 (persistent fork/remix CTA sticky sidebar) — that's the biggest remaining vision-aligned change on the detail page.
- Polish #3 (narrative step headers) becomes more visible once the Story-as-alert-box is gone — the dark `bg-surface-900 px-5 py-3` step header bars are now the heaviest remaining "system documentation" vocabulary on the page. Worth prioritizing.
- Backlog Structural #5 mentions "Polish #6 makes the CTA persistent" but the Polish queue never had a #6 (CTA-persistent is Polish #1). Pre-existing numbering drift from the 2026-04-17 queue reset; not mine to rewrite in this iteration but flagged for the next BACKLOG restock.

**Files touched:** `src/app/prompt/[id]/page.tsx`, `BACKLOG.md`, `ITERATION_LOG.md`.

## Iter 53 — 2026-04-17 — Result-first Browse card (Polish #1)

**What shipped.** `src/components/PromptCard.tsx` and `src/components/Skeleton.tsx` rewritten so the **outcome** — what the author actually built — is now the dominant visual block on every card. A new `resolveOutcome(prompt)` helper resolves a preview string in priority order: `prompt.result_content?.trim()` → last step's `result_content?.trim()` → `null` (no hero). When an outcome exists, the card opens with a hairline `bg-gradient-to-br from-brand-orange/55 via-surface-200 to-brand-blue/55 p-[1.5px]` gradient frame around a white inner panel (`px-4 py-3.5 min-h-[120px]` regular, `px-5 py-4 sm:px-6 sm:py-5 min-h-[140px]` featured) — borrows directly from iter 51's detail-page Final-output hero so the two surfaces share visual vocabulary. Quiet eyebrow row renders a blue 1.5×1.5 dot + `text-[9px] font-bold uppercase tracking-[0.14em]` **Outcome** + `·` + meta (either `what they shipped` for top-level payloads or `from step N of M` for step fallback). Body is `line-clamp-3` `whitespace-pre-line` at `text-[14px]` regular / `text-[15px] sm:text-[16px]` featured. Title/description/category moved BELOW the hero as supporting scaffolding with smaller scale (title `text-[15px]` with outcome, `text-base`/`text-xl` fallback without). Removed: the chevron-separated step-number chip strip (iter 26–30 era) and the "N steps" Layers chip (iter 29) — both were process-diagram vocabulary the detail-page journey strip (iter 50) already covers. Footer collapses to one typographic line: `difficulty · model` left, `by author · ↑votes · ⌘bookmarks` right, with `·` separators on `sm+` and author hidden on mobile. Skeleton updated to match: outcome-hero placeholder (gradient-free gray panel at `min-h-[120px]`), category eyebrow, short title, 2-line description, difficulty+model footer — replaces the old step-flow + badge-row skeleton shape so the Suspense fallback no longer telegraphs a layout that won't render.

**Why this approach (design rationale).** Backlog #1 was explicit: the OUTCOME block was buried below title/description/step-flow, and the card must sell the PROJECT, not the step-count. Three alternatives considered for where the outcome goes and how it's framed. (a) Keep outcome as a left-border callout inside the existing card stack but move it to position 1 — rejected because just moving a callout up still reads as "quote pulled from a page," not "this is the exhibit." (b) Render outcome on a tinted surface (faint orange wash) to carry brand weight — rejected because featured cards already carry an orange-wash body background, and a tinted outcome inside a tinted card collapses to a single flat orange zone. (c) Adopt the iter-51 gradient-frame treatment at card scale — chose this. The gradient border ties browse and detail into one "editorial exhibit" vocabulary, and white-on-white inside a gradient frame reads as content-first. Divergence from Vercel's gallery (WebFetched, see references): Vercel leads with an IMAGE as the dominant block. PathForge has no image upload yet (Structural #1 blocks that). Until images ship, the outcome prose IS the preview — a written exhibit stands in for a screenshot. When image uploads land, the gradient frame becomes the natural container for a 16:9 image (Structural #3 in the queue points at exactly that slot), and the prose preview becomes a secondary treatment or an image-caption-style subtitle. Also considered keeping the step-flow chips muted below the hero as a micro-flow indicator; rejected because iter 50's journey strip is the explicit place for "this is a chained build" and the card should resist re-inviting process vocabulary. On the meta string: `what they shipped` for top-level results frames the outcome as the author's declared ending; `from step N of M` for step-fallback signals "this is the last thing that happened" without lying that it's the declared outcome.

**References consulted.** `WebFetch https://vercel.com/templates` — confirmed the canonical gallery pattern: preview (image) at top as dominant visual, title next, tertiary metadata last. PathForge's card now matches this hierarchy with prose-as-preview until image upload ships. Linear's changelog and the iter-51 PathForge hero are the other two references informing the gradient-frame choice (already cited in iter 51).

**Responsive / edge-case coverage.** Featured cards get `p-6` padding and a larger outcome panel; regular cards get `p-5` and a more compact panel — both breathe on mobile because neither uses mobile-specific breakpoints for padding. `line-clamp-3` ensures long results don't blow out grid row heights. `whitespace-pre-line` preserves author line breaks in the outcome preview. Featured pill (`bg-brand-orange text-white`) stays above the gradient frame — acts as a gallery label, not a layered sticker. Edge cases handled: (1) project has `result_content` → hero sources from it, meta = "what they shipped"; (2) project has no `result_content` but steps with `result_content` → hero falls back to last-step result, meta = "from step N of M"; (3) project has neither → hero block entirely skipped, card falls back to title-led layout with bumped title size (`text-xl` featured / `text-base` regular) so it doesn't collapse to a metadata-only block; (4) category missing → eyebrow row simply omits, spacing gracefully tightens; (5) long author name → `truncate max-w-[8rem]` on the `by …` span keeps footer on one line. Focus-visible: inherits site-standard `outline-2 outline-brand-orange outline-offset-2` on the whole Link. Hover: regular cards get a top-edge orange scale-in line + `shadow-md -translate-y-px`; featured cards get `shadow-lg -translate-y-0.5` on their left-border accent — both preserved from prior iterations.

**Verification scope.** `npx tsc --noEmit` passes clean. `npm run build` passes clean — all 10 static pages generated, types pass. Dev server verified across five PromptCard render surfaces via curl + grep scan (Chrome MCP bridge was stale from prior-session carry-over; build-only + curl-surface verify per SKILL fallback): `/browse` → 20 cards × 1 `>Outcome<` = 20 outcome heroes, 40 `what they shipped` (all top-level sourced), 0 `from step ` (no fallback hits — all seeds have `result_content`), 0 `ChevronRight` / 0 `Layers` / 0 `bg-surface-50 border-b` (removed step-flow chips confirmed absent); `/` → 6 outcome heroes on the landing Featured/Recent block; `/browse?category=finance` → 2 cards, outcome heroes present; `/browse?q=email` → 2 cards, outcome heroes present; `/prompt/...3314` → detail page's "More in 💰 Finance & Accounting" section renders 3 sibling cards with outcome heroes, and the detail page's own structure (iter 50's Journey strip, iter 51's Final output hero) is still intact. Skeleton rewrite inspected by diff; Suspense fallback now matches the new card silhouette (gradient-free placeholder, category eyebrow strip, short title, 2-line description, difficulty+model footer). The `/prompt/new` redirect to login still fires (auth-gated write path unaffected).

**Follow-ups spotted.**
- Outcome preview at `line-clamp-3` works for most seeds but clamps mid-sentence when the first line is short (e.g. "$48,200 MRR\n\n..." — the blank-line feeds into the clamp as two visible lines). Future iteration could detect an empty second line and render the first paragraph only, or swap to a character-count cap with ellipsis — but that's a precision-tune, not a structural iteration.
- The gradient frame is identical across regular and featured cards. If visitor feedback ever flags "the featured distinction feels thin" (since iter-53 dropped the internal orange accents), consider shifting the frame to a brighter orange → blue gradient on featured cards only, or increasing featured min-h to 160px. Not worth doing speculatively.
- When image upload (Structural #1) lands, Browse card top becomes a 16:9 image container (Structural #3). The gradient frame is the natural outer border for that slot; outcome prose moves to a subtitle below the image or behind an image-absent fallback. Schema-wise the path is already clear.

**Files touched:** `src/components/PromptCard.tsx`, `src/components/Skeleton.tsx`, `BACKLOG.md`, `ITERATION_LOG.md`.

## Iter 52 — 2026-04-17 — Demote CodeBlock for natural-language step content (Polish #1)

**What shipped.** Added a new sibling `<Prose>` component (`src/components/Prose.tsx`) and a new classifier (`src/lib/content-kind.ts`) that auto-selects between CodeBlock (dark mono panel) and Prose (light editorial card) per step payload. The detail page (`src/app/prompt/[id]/page.tsx`) now routes every step prompt, step result, and single-prompt-branch through a `<StepContent>` dispatcher that calls `detectContentKind` and picks the right renderer. `<Prose>` shape: white card with hairline `border-surface-200`, quiet eyebrow row (accent dot + small-caps `tracking-[0.16em]` label + optional meta), reading-weight sans body at `text-[15px] leading-[1.7] text-surface-800` with `whitespace-pre-line` and `max-w-prose`, and a ghost `CopyButton` (new third variant) positioned `absolute top-2.5 right-2.5` that fades in on hover/focus. Heuristic signals that flip to `code`: presence of ` ``` ` fence, HTML-ish tags >25% of lines, `;` line-endings >30%, brace-only lines >15%, or dense indentation >50% of lines (only when ≥4 lines). Defaults to `prose` — step content on PathForge is overwhelmingly natural language (14/14 mock-data step payloads classify as prose, verified via an inline node sanity test). Also added a third `ghost` variant to `CopyButton` (white-on-white with hairline border, label hidden at rest, appears on `copied` state) so Prose's copy affordance doesn't compete with the body text.

**Why this approach (design rationale).** Backlog offered a choice: overload CodeBlock with a `naturalLanguage` prop, or ship a sibling `<Prose>`. Chose the sibling. CodeBlock's name carries semantic weight — "code" in the identifier tells the next reader what it renders. A CodeBlock in natural-language mode would be a branchy component where half the codepaths don't render as code, making callsites harder to reason about and defeating the documentation value of the name. A sibling forces the callsite to declare intent, and `<StepContent>` — a tiny dispatcher — centralizes the selection logic so no future detail page picks the wrong component. I also considered rendering Prose with a light surface color (`surface-50` or faint orange tint) instead of pure white. Rejected: the step card already has a `bg-surface-900` header bar and sits on the page's white body background; a tinted Prose inside a white-bodied card would introduce a third subtle-surface tone in the same 400px viewport stretch. Pure white keeps the Prose panel legible as "content, not chrome." On copy-button placement: tried putting it in the eyebrow row inline next to the meta; rejected because the eyebrow is quiet-by-design and a button at rest there pulls the eye from the body. Absolute-positioned ghost-fade lets the prose breathe by default and surfaces the action exactly when the reader's cursor is already in the block. On the label prop: kept "prompt"/"result" for the iter-52 scope — renaming to "ask"/"approach" is Polish #3 in the queue, explicitly a separate iteration. Shipping both at once would couple a component refactor with a copy rewrite and make the log less useful to future-me. Heuristic tuning: the dense-indentation signal originally fired at >30% of lines, which misclassified a prose block with a bulleted list ("    • one", "    • two", ...) as code. Bumped to >50% AND requires ≥4 lines — short prose with a trailing indent doesn't fire. The node sanity test covers that case (`Mostly natural language but the second line happens to be indented a bit.` → prose).

**References consulted.** `WebFetch https://linear.app/changelog` succeeded and confirmed the pattern: Linear presents long-form prose "without explicit framing — long-form text blocks lack visible borders or background colors… [relying on] typographic hierarchy, whitespace, and subtle semantic differentiation." My Prose diverges deliberately by keeping a hairline border, because PathForge's detail page sits multiple Prose blocks directly adjacent inside a step card (prompt + result, then prompt + result of the next step), and totally un-framed blocks would read as one continuous paragraph rather than as distinct contributions. A hairline surface-200 border is the minimum edge-weight that preserves "block-ness" without competing with content. `WebFetch https://read.cv` returned HTTP 402 (bot/paywall block) — attempt noted, didn't cite. `WebFetch https://docs.stripe.com/` returned only navigation chrome — attempt noted, didn't cite. Two of three references fetched; SKILL's floor (don't hard-halt if all three fail) wasn't reached. On the ghost CopyButton: Raycast's command-row "copy" affordance surfaces on hover and hides at rest — that's the behavior I borrowed (opacity-0 → opacity-100 on `group-hover` and `focus-within`).

**Responsive / edge-case coverage.** Prose padding is `px-5 pt-2.5 pb-5` — narrow mobile stays readable without breakpoint variants (no `sm:px-8` jump that'd introduce a visual shift at 640px). Body font size at `text-[15px]` is a deliberate notch below CodeBlock's `text-[13px]` — prose reads longer than monospace so needs more x-height; 15px is the site's Linear-like editorial-body size (matches the PromptCard description). `max-w-prose` caps the measure at ~656px so a very long result on a wide step card doesn't read as a wall. `whitespace-pre-line` preserves author line breaks; `min-w-0` not needed because the parent step-card already clips overflow. Focus handling: the `CopyButton` ghost variant retains the site-standard `outline-brand-orange focus-visible` ring (inherited from the variant switch in CopyButton.tsx), and the Prose wrapper uses `focus-within:opacity-100` so keyboard-focusing the button reveals it even without a pointer hover. Edge cases handled explicitly:
- Empty/whitespace-only content → detector returns 'prose' (empty text is vacuously prose; CodeBlock would render an empty dark panel which reads worse).
- Markdown-fenced code (e.g. a JSON blob inside a prose explanation) → flips the whole payload to `code` because inside a fence is the strongest "treat me as literal" signal; the prose explanation around it is a small price for the fence's hard guarantee.
- Mixed-kind payloads (prose with inline `if (x) { y }`) → single occurrences don't trip the detector because every signal uses a ratio against total line count, not absolute count.
- Short prose (1–3 lines) → dense-indent signal is gated behind ≥4 lines so tightly-formatted short prose doesn't false-flag.
- Details/disclosure container already existed from iter 49; Prose renders correctly inside the nested `<details>` (the open/close toggle is on an outer `group` wrapper, Prose has its own `group/prose` for its own hover interactions — no collision because of the slash-namespaced Tailwind group syntax).

**Verification scope.** `npx tsc --noEmit` passes clean. `npm run build` passes clean — all 10 static pages generated, TypeScript pass in 1.76s. Inline Node sanity test (`/tmp/kind-test.mjs`) runs 9 hand-authored cases (prose w/ paragraphs, prose w/ numbered list, fenced JSON, JS function w/ semicolons, HTML fragment, bare JSON, short prose w/ single indented line, all-indented block) — 9/9 pass. Mock-data scan (`/tmp/kind-mock.mjs` against `src/lib/mock-data.ts`) — extracted 14 template-literal `content:` / `result_content:` fields, 14/14 classify as prose, 0/14 as code. This is the expected distribution for PathForge's current seed data; validates that the common case goes to Prose without needing per-field author overrides. Chrome MCP verify attempted — `tabs_context_mcp` created a new tab (id 1834517331) but reported URL stuck on `chrome://newtab/` after two `navigate` calls, and `read_page` / `javascript_tool` returned "Cannot access a chrome:// URL" on both attempts. Extension bridge is reporting stale tab state (or Drew's Chrome isn't letting the extension drive navigation this session). **Chrome unreachable — build-only verify** per SKILL.md; the iteration ships and the next human review is more important. The separate `npm run build` was the backup path and completed clean.

**Follow-ups spotted.**
- Polish #3 in the queue was already pointing at renaming `label="prompt"`/`"result"` to `"ask"`/`"approach"` on the prose path. Now that Prose is live, that rename is the natural next iteration — and I've updated the backlog entry to call out Prose specifically.
- The `StepContent` dispatcher lives inline in `prompt/[id]/page.tsx`. If a third surface ever needs the same prose-vs-code auto-routing (builder preview rail already exists for the form; user-profile cards might eventually too), extract it to `src/components/StepContent.tsx`. Not worth doing speculatively for one callsite.
- Heuristic is conservative: a prose block that quotes a single curly-braced JSON literal (`{"key": "value"}`) on its own line can trip the brace-only detector once that one line exceeds 15% of total lines in a short payload. Acceptable trade-off for now (the payload really is more code-like than prose-like when JSON dominates), but a future iteration with real user data might want to add a small "manual override" toggle per-step in the builder — which is already Structural #4 in the queue.
- Ghost CopyButton at rest is truly invisible on white. Some users may not know to hover. Considered adding a very faint idle state (`opacity-30` at rest instead of `0`), but that re-introduces the "tiny chip at the top-right of every prose block" visual noise the whole point of this iteration was to avoid. If telemetry ever shows low copy-engagement on prose blocks, revisit.

**Files touched:** `src/components/Prose.tsx` (new), `src/lib/content-kind.ts` (new), `src/app/prompt/[id]/page.tsx`, `src/app/prompt/[id]/CopyButton.tsx`, `BACKLOG.md`, `ITERATION_LOG.md`.

## Iter 51 — 2026-04-17 — Case-study "Final output" hero above The Story (Polish #1)

**What shipped.** Inserted a new `<section aria-labelledby="final-output-eyebrow">` between the fork CTA (line 174 of `src/app/prompt/[id]/page.tsx`) and The Story. The hero resolves `heroContent = prompt.result_content?.trim() || lastStepWithResult?.result_content?.trim() || null` and renders only when a substantive output exists. Frame: a hairline gradient border — `bg-gradient-to-br from-brand-orange/55 via-surface-200 to-brand-blue/55 p-[1.5px]` around an inner `bg-white px-6 py-8 sm:px-10 sm:py-12 min-h-[220px] flex flex-col` card. Eyebrow is "Final output" with a blue 6×6 dot in mono/uppercase/tracking-[0.18em] style, followed by a `·` separator and a meta — either `what they shipped` (when sourcing from `prompt.result_content`) or an in-page anchor link `from step N of M` (when falling back to the last step's `result_content`). The body paragraph renders at `text-lg sm:text-xl text-surface-900 leading-[1.55] whitespace-pre-line max-w-prose` — no `CodeBlock`, no mono, no dark-editor chrome. Legacy bottom "The Result" section (was `border-l-4 border-brand-blue` callout at old line 363–374) removed entirely since it was double-rendering the same payload. Also dropped the `ArrowDown` import usage at the old Result H2 (still used inter-step, so kept in the import list). The Story keeps its orange callout — intentional, so the hero's editorial-gradient card doesn't compete with a parallel editorial box right below it (Polish #7 will revisit The Story's callout).

**Why this approach (design rationale).** The backlog entry offered two directions: "a dark panel with subtle orange→blue gradient border, or a generous editorial card." Considered both. Rejected the dark panel because the page already carries heavy dark weight — the header strip is `bg-surface-900`, every step card has a `bg-surface-900` header bar, and every `CodeBlock` in the Build Path is a dark mono panel. Adding a third dark surface above The Story would read as yet another "code thing" and defeat the "this is a build showcase, not a prompt library" vision anchor. The editorial white card with a hairline gradient edge is the opposite move — it borrows the site's orange→blue spine vocabulary (same gradient already lives in the vertical step pipe and the journey strip from iter 50) but applies it as a picture-frame edge rather than a surface fill, keeping the content light-on-white and reading as a magazine feature's primary exhibit. Also considered putting the hero INSIDE the existing `header` block right under the pills (tighter coupling to the title group). Rejected because then the fork CTA gets visually buried behind the hero, and the CTA is the single highest-intent button on the page per backlog Polish #3. Placing the hero *after* the CTA keeps the "read title → scan metadata → hit fork OR keep scrolling → see the output" flow intact. Fallback meta wording matters too: the `from step N of M` link is a real `<a href="#step-N">` so a reader can jump to where the output came from in the chain — this is the opposite of hiding the source, it's making the chain navigable from the hero.

**References consulted.** `WebFetch https://read.cv` returned HTTP 402 (paywall/bot block) — attempt noted, couldn't cite. `WebFetch https://linear.app/changelog` worked: confirmed the pattern I wanted — hero visual sits below title/subtitle with NO visible border or frame, "clean, minimal styling with slight drop shadows for depth," body prose follows. I diverged from the no-border path intentionally: Linear's pattern assumes a literal screenshot or video where the content IS the visual. PathForge's "final output" is usually prose, so an unframed block would just look like a floating paragraph and disappear. A hairline gradient frame gives the prose block enough edge-weight to read as "an exhibit" without fighting the content inside. `WebFetch https://vercel.com/templates` returned a generic description (their HTML structure didn't expose CSS details), so I couldn't cite specific treatment — noted, not load-bearing for this choice. The shadow I did add — `shadow-[0_1px_2px_rgba(15,23,42,0.04)]` — is the Linear "slight drop shadow for depth" move, restrained.

**Responsive / edge-case coverage.** Hero uses `px-6 py-8 sm:px-10 sm:py-12` so mobile gets 24×32px padding and desktop 40×48px — scales without breakpointing the frame itself. Body text steps `text-lg` → `sm:text-xl` so mobile reads at 18px and desktop at 20px. Eyebrow row uses `flex flex-wrap items-center gap-x-2.5 gap-y-1.5` so the "Final output · from step 3 of 3" meta wraps to a second row on very narrow widths rather than pushing off-screen. `whitespace-pre-line` preserves the author's intentional line breaks in `result_content` (mock data uses explicit `\n` formatting throughout). Focus-visible outline on the step-link fallback (`hover:text-brand-blue transition-colors duration-200` — matches the site's blue-is-result vocabulary). Edge cases handled:
- Project has `result_content` → hero sources from it, bottom "The Result" is already gone (removed wholesale), no duplication.
- Project has no `result_content` but has steps with results → hero falls back to `lastStepWithResult`, meta shows `from step N of M` as a jump link. The step card *also* shows the same payload inside its `CodeBlock`, but that's acceptable: the hero positions it above-the-fold as editorial prose; the step view keeps it as the formal result within the chain. Two contexts, two treatments, one payload.
- Project has neither → hero doesn't render (whole `{heroContent && (...)}` guard), page goes straight from fork CTA to The Story as before.
- Whitespace-only `result_content` → `?.trim() || null` rejects it, falls back or hides.

**Verification scope.** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean. `npm run build` clean — full production build succeeded, all 10 static pages generated, TypeScript typecheck passed. Chrome MCP on `/prompt/...3314` (3-step project with top-level result): accessibility tree confirms order `banner (title/pills/fork CTA) → region [ref_64] (Final output + what they shipped + body) → region [ref_68] (The Story) → region [ref_71] (Build Path)` — hero renders between fork CTA and The Story exactly as intended; legacy bottom "The Result" heading absent from a11y tree (successful removal). Chrome MCP on `/browse`: 20 projects, "Browse Projects" heading, Featured section (2 highlighted), "All Projects (18 total)" section, filters/sort intact — no regressions since the change was scoped to `prompt/[id]/page.tsx`. `curl http://localhost:3000/prompt/...3314 | grep` confirmed `aria-labelledby="final-output-eyebrow"` + `Final output` + `what they shipped` + hero body text all present in the streamed HTML; `border-l-4 border-brand-blue` (the old Result section marker) absent. Pre-existing `Failed to fetch` console exception on the detail page (unconfigured-Supabase artifact carried since iter 41, documented in iters 48/49/50) is still present and unrelated to structure-addition work. Note on Chrome MCP sidebar: the extension's `javascript_tool` returned `offsetHeight: 0` for all page elements in this session — investigation showed the extension was reading an alternate DOM branch (React streaming template subtree), not the visible rendered tree. `read_page` (a11y CDP path) worked correctly and was the source of truth for verification; `curl`-served HTML corroborated. Flagged as a tool-noise observation, not a rendering regression.

**Follow-ups spotted.**
- The Story section directly below the hero still lives in the `bg-primary-50/60 border-l-4 border-brand-orange` callout box. With the hero now a light editorial card and The Story sitting immediately below as an orange callout, the two treatments are adjacent but speak different dialects (magazine-exhibit vs documentation-alert). Polish #7 (in the queue) is exactly this — dropping The Story's callout for generous editorial prose would make the hero→story→build-path sequence read as one coherent feature article rather than three unrelated blocks.
- The hero body currently renders *all* of `result_content` unclamped at `text-xl`. For projects with very long results (several of the mock fixtures have 400+ word results with code fences), the hero expands to dominate the whole viewport and push The Story well below the fold — which over-weights the hero. Future iteration could add a `line-clamp-[12]` with a "Read full output" disclosure button, or detect code-fenced content and switch treatment. Not in scope for a structural iteration.

**Files touched:** `src/app/prompt/[id]/page.tsx`, `BACKLOG.md`, `ITERATION_LOG.md`.
